Proof That Rest Is a Positive Attribute
Razi argues that motion and rest share the same essence (māhiyya) and thus both must be positive attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that rest is a positive (thubūtī) attribute because it shares its quiddity (māhiyya) with motion.

Core Idea
Motion and rest share the same essence; rest cannot be mere absence.

Razi presents a critical argument in kalām: rest is not merely the absence of motion but a real, positive attribute. He uses an observational change-of-state argument and a deeper analytical argument based on shared quiddity. This lesson walks through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Observe the body's change of state
Read the first part of the passage where Razi describes seeing one body become at rest after motion and vice versa. Notice that the body itself remains the same.
This is an empirical observation that both states occur in the same subject.
2
Understand the implication of alternation
Razi argues that because the body persists, both states must be real (existential) attributes. If one were merely the absence of the other, the alternation would be unreal.
3
Compare the definitions of motion and rest
Read the definitions: motion is being in a location after another location; rest is being in a location after the same location. Note that both involve 'being in a location'.
The only difference is what preceded.
4
Conclude from shared quiddity
Razi says the accidental difference (precedence) does not affect the shared quiddity. Since motion is positive, rest must also be positive.
This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا عرفت ذلك، فنقول: الدليل على أن السكون أمر وجودي أنا نرى الجسم الواحد يصير ساكنا بعد أن كان متحركا. وبالعكس. فتبدل هاتين الحالتين مع بقاء الذات في الحالتين يقتضي كون إحدى هاتين الحالتين أمرا وجوديا؛ وإذا ثبت ذلك لزم كون كل واحد منهما أمرا وجوديا. وذلك لأن الحركة عبارة عن الحصول في الحيز، بعد أن كانت في حيز آخر، والسكون عبارة عن الحصول في الحيز، بعد أن كان في نفس ذلك الحيز. فالحركة والسكون متساويان في تمام الماهية وإنما الاختلاف بينهما في كون الحركة مسبوقة بحالة أخرى، وكون السكون ليس كذلك. وكون الشيء مسبوقا بغيره، وصف عرضي. والأوصاف العرضية لا تقدح في اتحاد الماهية. فثبت أن الحركة والسكون متساويان في تمام الماهية والحقيقة فإذا كان أحدهما وصفا ثبوتيا لزم كون الآخر ثبوتيا قطعا. فثبت بما ذكرنا أن السكون وصف ثبوتي.
When you know that, we say: the proof that rest is an existential matter is that we see one and the same body become at rest after it was in motion, and vice versa. So the alternation of these two states with the persistence of the essence in both states necessitates that one of these two states be an existential matter; and if that is established, it necessarily follows that each one of them is an existential matter. That is because motion is an expression for being in a location after having been in another location, and rest is an expression for being in a location after having been in the very same location. So motion and rest are equal in complete quiddity (tamām al-māhiyya); the only difference between them is that motion is preceded by another state, and rest is not so. And a thing being preceded by another is an accidental description (waṣf ʿaraḍī). Accidental descriptions do not impair the unity of quiddity. So it is established that motion and rest are equal in complete quiddity and reality; therefore if one of them is a positive (thubūtī) description, it necessarily follows that the other is positive. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned that rest is a positive description.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a proof that rest is an existential (wujūdī) or positive (thubūtī) attribute. Razi provides two arguments: first, an observational argument: we see a single body changing from motion to rest and vice versa while the body itself remains. This alternation between two states with a persisting substratum indicates that both states are real attributes inhering in the body, because if one were merely the absence of the other, the alternation would not be a real change but merely a privation. Second, a more analytic argument: motion and rest are both defined as 'being in a location' (al-ḥuṣūl fī al-ḥayyiz), differing only in that motion is preceded by being in a different location, while rest is not. This difference is accidental; the core quiddity (māhiyya) is the same: occupying a location. Accidental features do not affect the essence. Since motion is undoubtedly a positive attribute (it involves real change and actual location), and rest shares the same quiddity, rest must also be a positive attribute. The conclusion is categorical: rest is a positive (thubūtī) description. This is a crucial step in Razi's overall argument against eternal rest.

Key Terms
حركة (ḥaraka)
سكون (sukūn)
ماهية (māhiyya)
ثبوتي (thubūtī)
عرضي (ʿaraḍī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think motion is positive and rest is merely its absence.
Correction: Razi shows that motion and rest share the same quiddity, so rest must also be positive.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Razi gives for concluding that both motion and rest are positive (thubūtī) attributes?
A) Because both are observed to cause physical effects.
B) Because they share the same complete quiddity (tamām al-māhiyya) and differ only in an accidental feature.
C) Because the philosophers agree that both are real.
D) Because the body remains the same during both states.

Key Takeaway
Rest is a positive (thubūtī) attribute because it shares its complete quiddity with motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your life, do you often treat moments of stillness (rest) as empty gaps between real activities? How would your daily attitude change if you genuinely believed, as Razi proves, that rest is a real, positive state—not just the absence of motion?
?
When you feel spiritually stagnant, do you see it as a lack of progress or as an opportunity for a different kind of presence? Razi argues that rest shares the same quiddity as motion—so how can you intentionally inhabit seasons of waiting as full and meaningful rather than empty?
?
What does it mean for your own self-understanding that change and stability are equally real? Are you more likely to define yourself by your movements or your rest? How can you honor both as positive aspects of your existence before God?

Why an Eternal Attribute Cannot Cease
Imam Razi responds to an objection about the ceasing of eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that an eternal positive attribute cannot cease because it is either necessary by itself or caused by the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes are either self-necessary or dependent on the Necessary, so non-existence is impossible.

In this passage, the author responds to an objection about whether an eternal attribute can cease to exist. The objector concedes that rest is a positive attribute but questions why it cannot cease. The answer provides a concise logical dichotomy: the eternal is either necessary by itself or an effect of the Necessary, both of which entail impossibility of non-existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp its flow. Then read the English translation to ensure you understand the meaning.
Pay attention to the structure: concession, question, answer.
2
Identify the objection and concession
Note that the author first concedes that rest is a positive attribute. The objector then asks why an eternal positive attribute cannot cease.
3
Analyze the answer's two-part argument
The answer divides the eternal attribute into two possibilities: it is either necessary by itself (wajib li-dhatihi) or caused by the Necessary (ma'lul). Explain why non-existence is impossible in both cases.
This is a standard kalam technique of exhaustive dichotomy.
4
Reflect on the implication for divine attributes
Consider how this reasoning applies to God's eternal attributes like knowledge or power. They cannot cease because they are eternal.
This argument defends the permanence of God's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سلمنا أن السكون أمر ثبوتي. فلم قلتم : إن الثابت الأزلي لا يزول؟ قوله : لأن ذلكم الأزلي إما أن يكون واجبًا لذاته، وإما أن يكون معلولاً لما يكون واجبًا لذاته. وعلى التقديرين، فإنه يلزم امتناع العدم عليه.
We concede that rest is a positive attribute. Why do you say that the eternal positive (al-thabit al-azali) cannot cease? He said: Because that eternal is either necessary by itself (wajib li-dhatihi) or an effect (ma'lul) of that which is necessary by itself. In both cases, impossibility of non-existence ('adam) upon it follows.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a short objection-answer. The objector concedes rest is positive but asks why it cannot cease. The answer is that if it is eternal, it must be either necessary by itself or caused by the Necessary Being, in both cases non-existence is impossible, so it cannot cease.

Key Terms
ثابت أزلي
واجب لذاته
معلول
عدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal attributes can cease because God has power over everything.
Correction: The passage argues that eternal existence entails necessity; non-existence is impossible because the eternal is either necessary by itself or caused by the Necessary, both of which exclude non-existence.

Checkpoint
Why does the answer say an eternal positive attribute cannot cease?
A) Because it is impossible.
B) Because it is either necessary or caused by the Necessary.
C) Because God preserves it.
D) Because it is not an accident.

Key Takeaway
An eternal attribute cannot cease to exist because its existence is either intrinsic necessity or derived necessity, both of which exclude non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's attributes—like His knowledge and mercy—are eternal and cannot cease, why do you sometimes act as if His mercy might run out? What would it mean for your daily trust in Him if you internalized this logical certainty?
?
The passage argues that an eternal attribute cannot cease because it is either intrinsic to Allah or necessarily sustained by Him. Does your heart find rest in the fact that Allah's justice and compassion are unchangeable? Or do you secretly fear that He might become angry in a way that contradicts His eternal mercy?
?
Consider one attribute of Allah that you rely on most (e.g., His provision, guidance, forgiveness). How does the truth that this attribute is eternally fixed impact your sense of security? Are you building your life on that unshakeable foundation, or on temporary things?

The Impossibility of Change in God's Knowledge
Razi argues against change in God's knowledge by showing it would entail change in His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi holds that God's knowledge of temporal events does not entail any change in God's essence.

Core Idea
God's knowledge never changes; it is eternal and unchanging.

In this passage, Razi tackles a common objection: if God knows events as they occur, does that mean His knowledge changes over time? He argues that such a change would imply a change in God's very essence, which is impossible. Let us examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Razi sets up a conditional scenario.
The passage starts with 'تعالى محال' which is a continuation of a previous point.
2
Identify the logical structure
Razi presents a hypothetical: if an accident occurs, then God is knowing of it at that time. This leads to a statement about before and after.
3
Understand the implication
If God goes from not knowing to knowing, that would imply a change (hadath) in God. But the opponent agrees that is impossible.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the doctrine
The conclusion: God's knowledge does not change. It is eternal and encompasses all things without temporal fluctuation.
This aligns with the Islamic creed of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى محال . ثم إنه إذا حصل ذلك الحادث، فإنه يصدق على الله تعالى أنه عالم بحصوله في ذلك الوقت. فإذن صدق على الله تعالى أنه ما كان عالما بحصوله في ذلك الوقت، ثم صار عالمًا بحصوله في ذلك الوقت. فلو اقتضى صدق هذه القضية، حدوث أمر وتجدد وصف لزم حدوث شيء في ذات الله وذلك عندكم محال.
Impossible. Then if that accident occurs, it is true of God that He is knowing of its occurrence at that time. So it is true of God that He was not knowing of its occurrence at that time, then became knowing of its occurrence at that time. If the truth of this proposition necessitated the occurrence of an event and the renewal of an attribute, it would entail the occurrence of something in the essence of God, and that is impossible according to you.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents an argument against the possibility of change in God's knowledge. It begins by stating a conditional: if an accident occurs, then God is described as knowing of its occurrence at that time. The implication is that before the accident, God was not knowing of it at that specific time, and afterwards He became knowing. The opponent argues that if such a statement were true, it would necessitate a change (hadath) in God's essence, which the opponent agrees is impossible. Thus the premise that God's knowledge changes is rejected. The argument is based on the principle that God's attributes are eternal and unchanging.

Key Terms
حادث
عالم
ذات الله
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge changes as events occur.
Correction: God's knowledge is eternal and unchanging; change is only in the relation between God's knowledge and temporal events, not in the knowledge itself.

Checkpoint
What does Razi argue would be impossible if God's knowledge changed from not knowing to knowing?
A) The occurrence of the accident.
B) The truth of the proposition.
C) Something occurring in God's essence.
D) The creation of the world.

Key Takeaway
Razi establishes that God's knowledge is eternal and unchanging; any perceived change is a change in the known objects, not in God's attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge of your every sin was complete and unchanging from eternity, what does that say about the depth of His mercy in still guiding you to repent today? How does this realization change the way you approach your next moment of weakness?
?
You claim to believe that God's knowledge never changes. Yet when you face a new crisis, do you act as if God has just discovered your situation and is now reacting? What would it look like for you to live today consistently with the belief that God already knew every detail before you were born?
?
The argument shows that any change in God is impossible. How does this truth confront the moments you feel God is distant or angry because of a recent sin? Are you projecting human, changeable emotions onto the Eternal? What one step can you take to anchor your trust in His unchanging knowledge and mercy?

The Possibility of an Eternal Ceasing Due to a Negative Condition
Razi presents an objection to the claim that an eternal thing cannot cease, using the concept of a negative condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's objection that an eternal thing can cease if its continued existence depends on a condition that is removed.

Core Idea
Eternal things can cease if they depend on removable conditions.

In this passage, Razi addresses a key objection against the claim that eternal things cannot perish. He argues that even if something is eternal, its continued existence might hinge on a condition that can cease. He uses the example of an eternal negative condition to show how an eternal effect could come to an end.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponent's position
The opponent argues that an eternal thing cannot cease because it is either self-necessary or an effect of a self-necessary being, making non-existence impossible.
This is the claim Razi intends to challenge.
2
See Razi's concession
Razi points out that they already accept that eternal non-existence can cease (e.g., the non-existence of the world before creation).
3
Follow Razi's proposed scenario
Razi suggests that a cause's effect might depend on an eternal negative condition. If that condition is removed, the effect ceases.
This is the core of the objection.
4
Consider the conclusion
When the eternal negative condition ceases, the effect necessarily ceases. Thus, an eternal thing can cease to exist.
5
Reflect on the strength of the objection
Razi calls this a strong objection because it shows that the permanence of an eternal thing is not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سلمنا أن السكون أمر ثبوتي. فلم قلتم : إن الثابت الأزلي لا يزول؟ قوله : لأن ذلكم الأزلي إما أن يكون واجبًا لذاته، وإما أن يكون معلولاً لما يكون واجبًا لذاته. وعلى التقديرين، فإنه يلزم امتناع العدم عليه. قلنا : أنتم سلمتم أن العدم الأزلي جائز الزوال، ولا يمتنع أيضًا أن يكون تأثير العلة في محلولها موقوفًا على شرط عدمي أزلي. إذا ثبت هذا، فنقول : لم لا يجوز أن يكون الواجب لذاته : علة لوجود ذلك الأزلي، إلا أن تأثيره في إيجابه كان موقوفًا على شرط عدمي أزلي، ثم إن ذلك الشرط العدمي الأزلي زال ولما زال شرط التأثير لا جرم زال الأثر. وهذا سؤال قوي.
We concede that rest is a positive thing. So why do you say that the eternal positive does not cease? He said: Because that eternal is either necessary in itself or an effect of what is necessary in itself. On both suppositions, non-existence is impossible for it. We said: You have conceded that eternal non-existence is subject to cessation, and it is also not impossible that the effect of a cause on its effect be dependent upon an eternal negative condition. If this is established, then we say: Why is it not possible that the Necessary in itself is a cause for the existence of that eternal, but its effect in producing it was dependent upon an eternal negative condition, then that eternal negative condition ceased, and when the condition of the effect ceased, the effect necessarily ceased. And this is a strong objection.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer regarding the claim that an eternal thing cannot cease to exist. The opponent argues that if something is eternal, it is either self-necessary or an effect of a self-necessary cause, and in both cases non-existence is impossible. Razi responds by noting that they already accept that eternal non-existence (like the non-existence of the world before creation) can cease. He then proposes a scenario: the self-necessary being (God) is the cause of the eternal thing, but His causation was conditional upon an eternal negative condition (e.g., the absence of a certain state). When that negative condition disappears, the condition for causation is removed, and the effect ceases. This is a strong objection against the claim that the eternal is imperishable.

Key Terms
أزلي
ثابت
واجب لذاته
معلول
علة
شرط عدمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If something is eternal, it cannot cease to exist.
Correction: Razi shows that an eternal thing can cease if its existence depends on a condition that can be removed.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's objection, what could cause an eternal thing to cease?
A) The essence of the Necessary in itself.
B) The removal of an eternal negative condition.
C) The occurrence of a positive accident.
D) The will of the creator without condition.

Key Takeaway
Razi's objection demonstrates that an eternal thing can cease if its existence depends on a removable condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything besides God is dependent on conditions that can change, what in your life are you holding onto as if it were permanent? How would your habits change if you truly believed that your job, health, or relationships could cease when their conditions are removed?
?
Razi argues that even an eternal thing can cease if its condition ceases. Your faith (īmān) is a positive state—what conditions are necessary for it to persist? Are you actively maintaining those conditions, or assuming it will remain on its own?
?
The concept of a 'negative condition' that ceases is about removing an obstacle. What negative conditions—like pride, distraction, or sin—might be blocking the full effect of God's guidance in your life? What would it take to remove them today?

Three Objections to the Eternal Never Ceasing
Razi presents three counterexamples to the claim that the eternal never ceases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three counterexamples Razi uses to challenge the principle that the eternal never ceases.

Core Idea
Eternal things can cease: knowledge, possibility, and abrogation prove it.

Razi presents three powerful objections to the claim that what is eternal cannot cease. These examples—God's knowledge that the world will exist, the possibility of initial creation, and the abrogation of divine rulings—are drawn from the nature of God's attributes and actions. They force us to reexamine the relationship between eternity and change in the divine context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Razi structures each objection with 'First', 'Second', 'Third'.
The passage is dense; take time to understand each point.
2
Identify the first objection
Focus on the first counterexample: God's knowledge that the world will exist. Ask: Why does this knowledge cease? How does this challenge the claim that the eternal never ceases?
The key is that the content of knowledge changes when the world exists.
3
Examine the second objection
Consider the possibility (sihha) of creating the world initially. After creation, this possibility no longer exists. Why is that a problem for the claim?
Possibility is an eternal attribute that ceases.
4
Understand the third objection
The third objection deals with abrogation (naskh). Razi argues that the abrogated ruling must be eternal, so its removal shows an eternal thing ceasing.
This objection ties into discussions of divine law.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how these three examples collectively refute the principle. What does this tell us about divine attributes and actions?
Razi uses these to defend the possibility of change in divine matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : قولكم الأزلي لا يزول منقوض بأمور : أحدها: أنه تعالى كان عالمًا في الأزل بأن العالم سيوجد، فإذا أوجده لم يبق علمه بأن العالم سيوجد ، وإلا كان ذلك جهلاً . فإذن علمه بأن العالم سيوجد أمر أزلي، مع أنه قد زال. وثانيها : أن الله تعالى كان موصوفًا في الأزل بأنه يصح منه إيجاد العالم ابتداء. ثم إذا أوجد الله تعالى العالم، استحال بعد ذلك أن يصح منه إيجاد العالم ابتداء وإلا لكان ذلك إيجاد الموجود. وإنه محال . فتلك الصحة: حكم أزلي وقد زال. وثالثها: أن النسخ عندكم عبارة عن رفع الحكم. وذلك الحكم المرفوع إما أن يقال : إنه كان حدثًا، أو كان قديما . والأول محال وإلا لزم كون ذات الله تعالى محلا للحوادث. فبقي القسم الثاني وهو أن ذلك الحكم المرفوع كان إذن قديما. فارتفاعه يكون زوالا للقديم.
Then we say: Your statement that the eternal does not cease is refuted by several matters: First: God was eternally knowing that the world will exist. When He brought it into existence, His knowledge that the world will exist no longer remains, otherwise that would be ignorance. So His knowledge that the world will exist is eternal, yet it has ceased. Second: God was eternally described as having the possibility of creating the world initially. Then when God created the world, it becomes impossible thereafter that He have the possibility of creating it initially, otherwise that would be creating what already exists, which is impossible. So that possibility is an eternal judgment, and it has ceased. Third: Abrogation (naskh) according to you is the lifting of a ruling. That lifted ruling is either said to be temporal (hadith) or eternal (qadim). The first is impossible because it would entail God's essence being a locus for temporal events. So the remaining possibility is that the lifted ruling was eternal. Its being lifted would then be the cessation of the eternal.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents three counterexamples to the principle that an eternal thing cannot cease. The first is God's knowledge that the world will exist: it is eternal but ceases when the world comes into existence, otherwise God would be ignorant. The second is the possibility (sihha) of God creating the world initially: it is eternal but ceases after creation, as it becomes impossible to create an already existing thing. The third is the abrogation of divine laws: the abrogated ruling must be eternal (since temporal rulings would imply change in God), so its abrogation means an eternal ruling has ceased. These examples directly challenge the claim that the eternal is imperishable.

Key Terms
أزلي
عالم
صحة
نسخ
حكم
قديم
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's knowledge of future events is unchanging, but Razi shows that the specific content (that the world will exist) ceases to be true after creation.
Correction: Razi's first objection demonstrates that the particular content of God's knowledge can change, even though His knowledge itself is eternal.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of Razi's counterexamples to the claim that the eternal never ceases?
A) God's knowledge that the world will exist.
B) The possibility of God creating the world initially.
C) The abrogation of a divine ruling.
D) The persistence of a body in motion.

Key Takeaway
Razi uses three examples—knowledge, possibility, and abrogation—to argue that eternal things can cease, challenging the principle of immutability of the eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is one thing in your life—a relationship, a status, a skill, or a certainty—that you treat as if it will never end, even though Razi's examples suggest that everything besides Allah is subject to cessation? What would change if you truly believed it could cease at any moment?
?
Razi argues that even God's knowledge of a specific future event ceases when that event occurs. Does this make you feel unsettled about the permanence of anything in your faith? Are you willing to trust a God whose knowledge 'changes' (in content) even if His essence does not?
?
If divine rulings can be abrogated, what does that say about your attachment to religious laws that you assume are final? Are you prepared for the possibility that Allah might lift or alter what you consider permanent, and how does that affect your submission to Him?

Divine Attributes

Counterexample 1: God's Eternal Knowledge Ceases
Razi's first counterexample: God's knowledge ceasing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's knowledge that the world would exist provides a counterexample to the claim that the eternal cannot cease.

Core Idea
God's eternal knowledge ceases after creation, proving the eternal can cease.

Imam Razi begins his refutation by pointing to a fundamental attribute of God: His knowledge. If the eternal cannot cease, then God's knowledge that the world will exist should remain forever. But once the world exists, that knowledge would become ignorance if it remained, so it must cease. This shows that an eternal attribute can indeed cease.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
The opponent claims that anything eternal cannot cease to exist. Razi tests this with God's knowledge.
2
Follow the logic
God knew eternally that the world would exist. After creation, that knowledge no longer applies. If it remained, it would be ignorance.
Notice the contradiction if it remained.
3
Draw the conclusion
Thus, an eternal attribute (God's knowledge) has ceased, refuting the premise.
This counterexample targets divine omniscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : قولكم الأزلي لا يزول منقوض بأمور : أحدها: أنه تعالى كان عالمًا في الأزل بأن العالم سيوجد، فإذا أوجده لم يبق علمه بأن العالم سيوجد ، وإلا كان ذلك جهلاً . فإذن علمه بأن العالم سيوجد أزلي، مع أنه قد زال. وثانيها : أن الله تعالى كان موصوفًا في الأزل بأنه يصح منه إيجاد العالم في لا يزال ابتداء. ثم إذا أوجد الله تعالى العالم، استحال بعد ذلك أن يصح منه إيجاد العالم ابتداء وإلا لكان ذلك إيجاد الموجود. وإنه محال . فتلك الصحة: حكم أزلي وقد زال. وثالثها: أن النسخ عندكم عبارة عن رفع الحكم. وذلك الحكم المرفوع إما أن يقال : إنه كان حدثًا، أو كان قديما . والأول محال وإلا لزم كون ذات الله تعالى محلا للحوادث. فبقي القسم الثاني وهو أن ذلك الحكم المرفوع كان إذن قديما. فارتفاعه يكون زوالا للقديم.
Then we say: Your statement that the eternal does not cease is refuted by matters: First: God Almighty was knowing in pre-eternity that the world would exist, and when He brought it into existence, His knowledge that the world would exist no longer remained, otherwise that would be ignorance. Thus His knowledge that the world would exist is eternal, yet it has ceased. Second: God Almighty was described in pre-eternity as it being possible for Him to originate the world initially. Then when God brought the world into existence, it becomes impossible after that for it to be possible for Him to originate the world initially, otherwise that would be bringing into existence what already exists, and that is impossible. So that possibility is an eternal judgment and it has ceased. Third: Abrogation (al-naskh) according to you is the removal of a ruling. That removed ruling must be said either to have been originated or to have been eternal. The first is impossible, otherwise it would necessitate that the essence of God be a locus for originated events. So the second division remains, which is that the removed ruling was therefore eternal. Its removal would be a ceasing of the eternal.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents three counterexamples to the claim that the eternal cannot cease. First: God's knowledge that the world would exist is eternal but ceases once the world exists, otherwise it would be ignorance. Second: God's attribute of being able to create the world initially is eternal but ceases after creation. Third: The concept of abrogation in Islamic law involves removing a ruling; if that ruling is eternal (as some opponents hold), then its removal is the ceasing of an eternal thing. These examples show that the premise is false.

Counterexample 2: The Possibility of Originating the World Ceases
Razi's second counterexample: possibility of originating ceasing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the eternal possibility of God originating the world ceasing refutes the claim that the eternal cannot cease.

Core Idea
God's eternal possibility to create initially ceases after creation, proving the eternal can cease.

Razi's second counterexample focuses on a divine attribute: the possibility (sihha) of originating the world from nothing. This attribute is eternal, but once the world exists, it no longer makes sense to say that God can originate it from nothing, as that would imply creating what already exists. Thus, an eternal judgment (hukm azali) about God ceases, disproving the premise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the attribute
In pre-eternity, God is described as having the possibility to originate the world initially, i.e., it is possible for Him to do so.
2
See the change after creation
Once the world exists, that possibility no longer holds, because originating something that already exists is impossible.
This shows the eternal judgment has ceased.
3
Conclude the refutation
Thus, an eternal attribute (the possibility) has ceased, showing that the eternal can cease.

Counterexample 3: Abrogation Involves Ceasing of an Eternal Ruling
Razi's third counterexample: abrogation and ceasing of eternal ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the concept of abrogation (naskh) provides a counterexample to the claim that the eternal cannot cease, by involving the ceasing of an eternal ruling.

Core Idea
Abrogation shows that an eternal ruling can cease, thus the eternal can cease.

Razi's third counterexample comes from the Islamic legal principle of abrogation (naskh). In some theological views, a ruling that is abrogated could be considered eternal (if it existed in God's knowledge from eternity). If so, then its removal would be the ceasing of an eternal thing. This undermines the claim that the eternal cannot cease, pointing to a real-life example in divine law.

Guided Path
1
Define abrogation
Abrogation is the removal of a ruling. The ruling that is removed must be either originated or eternal.
2
Analyze the eternal option
If the removed ruling is eternal, then its removal is the ceasing of an eternal thing.
This directly contradicts the premise.
3
Reject the originated option
If the ruling is originated, that would imply God's essence is a locus for originated events, which is impossible.
So the only consistent option is that the ruling is eternal.
4
Conclude
Therefore, abrogation involves the ceasing of an eternal ruling, providing a clear counterexample.

Source Text

The First Proof: Infinite Regress from Positive Necessity
Razi presents the first proof: if necessity were positive, it leads to infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's first proof that necessity cannot be a positive attribute because it leads to an infinite regress.

Core Idea
If necessity were positive, the Necessary Existent would require another necessity, ad infinitum.

Imam Razi begins his response to the objection that necessity (wujub) is a negative attribute. He presents the first of three proofs: if necessity were a positive attribute, it would lead to an infinite regress. This proof shows the absurdity of treating necessity as a real addition to the essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the structure of the proof. Notice the conditional 'if necessity were positive' and the two branches.
2
Identify the two branches
The proof splits into two cases: either the description of essence by existence is necessary or not. Each leads to an impossibility.
If not necessary → possibility; if necessary → regress.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Both branches are impossible, so the initial assumption that necessity is positive must be false. Therefore necessity is negative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الأول) فما الدليل على أن الوجوب ليس وصفًا سلبيًا ثم الذي يدل على أن الوجوب وصف سلبي وجوه : أحدها : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان مساويًا لسائر الموجودات في الوجود، ومخالفًا لها في ماهيتها المخصوصة وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة. فالوجود بالذات لو كان أمرًا ثبوتيًا لكانت ماهيته مغايرة لوجوده، فاتصاف ماهيته بوجوده إما أن يكون واجبًا وإما أن لا يكون، فإن لم يكن واجبًا كان الوجوب الذاتي ممكن الوجود لذاته، فكان الواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا لذاته، وذلك محال، وإن كان واجبًا فهذا الوجوب صفة لاتصاف تلك الماهية بذلك الوجود، فيكون وجوب ذلك الوجود مغايرا له، ويكون الكلام فيه كما في الأول، فيلزم التسلسل، وهو محال. وثانيهما : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان إما أن يكون عبارة عن تمام تلك الحقيقة المحكوم عليها بالوجوب، وإما أن يكون جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة، وإما أن يكون أمرًا خارجًا عن تلك الحقيقة، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فالقول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطل وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع أن يكون الوجوب تمام تلك الحقيقة والماهية وذلك لأن تلك الماهية محكوم عليها بأنها واجبة، والموضوع يمتنع أن يكون عين المحمول ؛ لأن ماهية واجب الوجود غير معلومة والمعلوم ليس هو نفس ما هو غير معلوم. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة لأن على هذا التقدير تكون تلك الحقيقة مركبة، وقد بيَّنتم أن كل مركب ممكن فإنه يلزم أن يكون الواجب لذاته ممكنا لذاته، وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة لأن كل ما كان صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة مفتقر إليها كان تحققه متوقفًا على تحقق تلك الحقيقة، وكل ما كان كذلك كان ممكنا لذاته، فذلك الوجوب بالذات ممكن لذاته، وإذا كان الوجوب ممكنا بالذات كان الواجب بالذات أولى بأن يكون ممكنا بالذات فثبت أن الأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فكان القول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطلا . وثالثها: أن الوجوب محمول على العدم والمحمول على العدم يمتنع أن يكون ثابتا، فالوجوب يمتنع أن يكون ثابتاً، وإنما قلنا إن الوجوب محمول على العدم لأن كل ما يصدق عليه أنه يمتنع أن يوجد يصدق عليه أنه يجب أن لا يوجد، فالوجوب
The first question: What is the proof that necessity (wujub) is not a negative attribute? Then that which indicates that necessity is a negative attribute are [several] aspects: One of them: That if necessity were a positive attribute, it would be equal to the rest of existents in existence and different from them in their specific essence, and that by which there is participation is different from that by which there is distinction. So if existence by essence (al-wujud bi al-dhat) were a positive thing, its essence would be different from its existence. Then the description of its essence by its existence is either necessary or not. If it is not necessary, then essential necessity (al-wujub al-dhati) would be possible in itself, and thus the necessary in itself would be more fitting to be possible in itself, which is impossible. And if it is necessary, then this necessity is an attribute of the description of that essence by that existence, so the necessity of that existence is different from it, and the discussion concerning it is as in the first, necessitating an infinite regress, which is impossible. The second: That if necessity were a positive attribute, it would either be identical to the whole of that reality which is judged to be necessary, or a part of that reality, or something external to that reality. All three divisions are false, so the statement that necessity is positive is false. We say that it is impossible for necessity to be the whole of that reality and essence because that essence is judged to be necessary, and the subject cannot be the same as the predicate because the essence of the Necessary Existent is unknown, and what is known is not the same as what is unknown. And we say that it is impossible for necessity to be a part of that reality because on this assumption that reality would be composite, and you have shown that every composite is possible, so the necessary in itself would be possible in itself. And we say that it is impossible for necessity to be an attribute external to the reality because everything that is an attribute external to the reality and dependent upon it has its realization contingent upon the realization of that reality, and everything like that is possible in itself. So that essential necessity would be possible in itself, and if necessity is possible in itself, then the necessary in itself is more fitting to be possible in itself. Thus it is established that the three divisions are false, and the statement that necessity is a positive thing is false. The third: That necessity is predicated of non-existence, and what is predicated of non-existence cannot be a positive thing. So necessity cannot be positive. We say that necessity is predicated of non-existence because everything of which it is true that it is impossible for it to exist, it is true that it must not exist, so necessity...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct proofs that necessity (wujub) is a negative attribute (sifah salbiyyah) and not a positive (thubutiyyah) one. The first proof: If necessity were positive, then the Necessary Existent would have an essence distinct from its existence, leading to either contingency or an infinite regress, both absurd. The second proof: Necessity cannot be the whole of the essence (since subject and predicate differ), nor a part (making composite and thus possible), nor external (since that would make necessity dependent and thus possible). The third proof: Necessity is predicated of non-existence (e.g., it is necessary that a thing does not exist), and what is predicated of non-existence cannot be a positive attribute. These proofs collectively establish that necessity is a negative attribute, which is crucial for the earlier reply to the objection about composition.

Key Terms
الوجوب
وصف ثبوتي
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Necessity is a positive attribute like existence itself.
Correction: If necessity were positive, it would cause an infinite regress or make the Necessary Existent contingent. Therefore, necessity is a negative attribute, i.e., the negation of possibility or dependence.

Checkpoint
What does the first proof conclude from the assumption that necessity is positive?
A) It leads to a contradiction only if the description is not necessary.
B) It leads to infinite regress only if the description is necessary.
C) It leads to impossibility in both branches: either possibility or infinite regress.
D) It proves that necessity is a positive attribute.

Key Takeaway
The first proof demonstrates that treating necessity as a positive attribute forces an infinite regress or self-contradiction, so necessity must be negative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If necessity were a positive attribute, the Necessary Existent would depend on another necessity to connect its essence to existence. How does this logical impossibility deepen your awe of God's absolute independence? What personal dependencies are you clinging to that you need to let go of, trusting only in His self-sufficiency? Take a moment to identify one area and commit to detaching from it.
?
The proof shows that an infinite regress of necessities is impossible. In your life, you may be chasing an endless chain of approvals, achievements, or validations. Where do you see yourself in an infinite regress of seeking value from created things? How can truly internalizing that only God is the ultimate Necessary stop that cycle? What will you do this week to break one link in that chain?
?
Razi argues that necessity is not a positive attribute but rather a negation of contingency. This means God's necessity is not an added quality but a fundamental reality. When you describe God as 'Necessary', do you subconsciously treat it as an attribute alongside others, or do you let it define your entire understanding of Him? What would change in your worship if you truly felt that everything else is contingent and fleeting?

The Second Proof: Necessity Cannot Be a Positive Attribute in Three Ways
Razi enumerates and refutes three possibilities for necessity as a positive attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's second proof that necessity is not a positive attribute by showing it cannot be the whole, part, or external to the essence.

Core Idea
Necessity is neither the essence itself, nor a part of it, nor an external addition — so it must be negative.

In the second proof, Razi systematically eliminates all possibilities for necessity to be a positive attribute. He argues that necessity cannot be identical to the essence, nor a component of it, nor something added to it. Each option leads to contradiction, proving that necessity must be a negative description.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that Razi lists three possibilities for necessity as a positive attribute: whole, part, or external.
2
Understand the refutation of 'whole'
Razi argues that the subject (essence) cannot be the same as the predicate (necessity) because the essence of the Necessary is unknown.
3
Understand the refutation of 'part'
If necessity were a part, the essence would be composite, and every composite is possible — contradicting necessity.
4
Understand the refutation of 'external'
If necessity were external, it would depend on the essence, making it possible — again contradicting necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الأول) فما الدليل على أن الوجوب ليس وصفًا سلبيًا ثم الذي يدل على أن الوجوب وصف سلبي وجوه : أحدها : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان مساويًا لسائر الموجودات في الوجود، ومخالفًا لها في ماهيتها المخصوصة وما به المشاركة مغاير لما به المباينة. فالوجود بالذات لو كان أمرًا ثبوتيًا لكانت ماهيته مغايرة لوجوده، فاتصاف ماهيته بوجوده إما أن يكون واجبًا وإما أن لا يكون، فإن لم يكن واجبًا كان الوجوب الذاتي ممكن الوجود لذاته، فكان الواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا لذاته، وذلك محال، وإن كان واجبًا فهذا الوجوب صفة لاتصاف تلك الماهية بذلك الوجود، فيكون وجوب ذلك الوجود مغايرا له، ويكون الكلام فيه كما في الأول، فيلزم التسلسل، وهو محال. وثانيهما : أن الوجوب لو كان وصفًا ثبوتيًا لكان إما أن يكون عبارة عن تمام تلك الحقيقة المحكوم عليها بالوجوب، وإما أن يكون جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة، وإما أن يكون أمرًا خارجًا عن تلك الحقيقة، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فالقول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطل وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع أن يكون الوجوب تمام تلك الحقيقة والماهية وذلك لأن تلك الماهية محكوم عليها بأنها واجبة، والموضوع يمتنع أن يكون عين المحمول ؛ لأن ماهية واجب الوجود غير معلومة والمعلوم ليس هو نفس ما هو غير معلوم. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب جزءًا من تلك الحقيقة لأن على هذا التقدير تكون تلك الحقيقة مركبة، وقد بيَّنتم أن كل مركب ممكن فإنه يلزم أن يكون الواجب لذاته ممكنا لذاته، وإنما قلنا إنه يمتنع كون الوجوب صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة لأن كل ما كان صفة خارجة عن الحقيقة مفتقر إليها كان تحققه متوقفًا على تحقق تلك الحقيقة، وكل ما كان كذلك كان ممكنا لذاته، فذلك الوجوب بالذات ممكن لذاته، وإذا كان الوجوب ممكنا بالذات كان الواجب بالذات أولى بأن يكون ممكنا بالذات فثبت أن الأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فكان القول بكون الوجوب أمرًا ثبوتيًا باطلا . وثالثها: أن الوجوب محمول على العدم والمحمول على العدم يمتنع أن يكون ثابتا، فالوجوب يمتنع أن يكون ثابتاً، وإنما قلنا إن الوجوب محمول على العدم لأن كل ما يصدق عليه أنه يمتنع أن يوجد يصدق عليه أنه يجب أن لا يوجد، فالوجوب
The first question: What is the proof that necessity (wujub) is not a negative attribute? Then that which indicates that necessity is a negative attribute are [several] aspects: One of them: That if necessity were a positive attribute, it would be equal to the rest of existents in existence and different from them in their specific essence, and that by which there is participation is different from that by which there is distinction. So if existence by essence (al-wujud bi al-dhat) were a positive thing, its essence would be different from its existence. Then the description of its essence by its existence is either necessary or not. If it is not necessary, then essential necessity (al-wujub al-dhati) would be possible in itself, and thus the necessary in itself would be more fitting to be possible in itself, which is impossible. And if it is necessary, then this necessity is an attribute of the description of that essence by that existence, so the necessity of that existence is different from it, and the discussion concerning it is as in the first, necessitating an infinite regress, which is impossible. The second: That if necessity were a positive attribute, it would either be identical to the whole of that reality which is judged to be necessary, or a part of that reality, or something external to that reality. All three divisions are false, so the statement that necessity is positive is false. We say that it is impossible for necessity to be the whole of that reality and essence because that essence is judged to be necessary, and the subject cannot be the same as the predicate because the essence of the Necessary Existent is unknown, and what is known is not the same as what is unknown. And we say that it is impossible for necessity to be a part of that reality because on this assumption that reality would be composite, and you have shown that every composite is possible, so the necessary in itself would be possible in itself. And we say that it is impossible for necessity to be an attribute external to the reality because everything that is an attribute external to the reality and dependent upon it has its realization contingent upon the realization of that reality, and everything like that is possible in itself. So that essential necessity would be possible in itself, and if necessity is possible in itself, then the necessary in itself is more fitting to be possible in itself. Thus it is established that the three divisions are false, and the statement that necessity is a positive thing is false. The third: That necessity is predicated of non-existence, and what is predicated of non-existence cannot be a positive thing. So necessity cannot be positive. We say that necessity is predicated of non-existence because everything of which it is true that it is impossible for it to exist, it is true that it must not exist, so necessity...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct proofs that necessity (wujub) is a negative attribute (sifah salbiyyah) and not a positive (thubutiyyah) one. The first proof: If necessity were positive, then the Necessary Existent would have an essence distinct from its existence, leading to either contingency or an infinite regress, both absurd. The second proof: Necessity cannot be the whole of the essence (since subject and predicate differ), nor a part (making composite and thus possible), nor external (since that would make necessity dependent and thus possible). The third proof: Necessity is predicated of non-existence (e.g., it is necessary that a thing does not exist), and what is predicated of non-existence cannot be a positive attribute. These proofs collectively establish that necessity is a negative attribute, which is crucial for the earlier reply to the objection about composition.

Key Terms
الوجوب
وصف ثبوتي
ماهية
مركب
ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Necessity is an additional quality that inheres in the Necessary Existent.
Correction: If necessity were an additional quality, it would have to be either the same as the essence, a part of it, or separate from it — all impossible. Hence necessity is a negative concept, not a positive attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, why can necessity not be a part of the essence?
A) Because the subject and predicate must be the same.
B) Because compositeness implies possibility.
C) Because it would lead to infinite regress.
D) Because the essence is unknown.

Key Takeaway
The second proof eliminates all logical ways for necessity to be a positive attribute, leaving only the conclusion that it is negative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own existence, do you ever treat your absolute dependence on Allah as if it were just an external quality added to your life, rather than the very definition of your being? How does Razi's argument that necessity cannot be external challenge your self-perception?
?
If you truly believed that composite things are inherently possible (contingent), would your attachment to the material world and its 'composite' structures change? Would you still cling to what is transient?
?
Razi says the essence of the Necessary is unknown, yet we claim to know He is necessary. Are you content to know Allah through His attributes alone, without needing to grasp His essence? Or does your heart secretly long for a direct vision that He has not granted?

The Third Proof: Necessity Predicated of Non-Existence (Incomplete)
Razi begins the third proof: necessity is predicated of non-existence, so it cannot be positive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the starting premise of Razi's third proof that necessity is a negative attribute because it is predicated of non-existence.

Core Idea
Necessity can be said of non-existence, showing it is not a positive attribute.

In this third proof, Razi introduces a different angle: necessity is predicated of non-existence (e.g., 'it is necessary that a thing does not exist'). Since what is predicated of non-existence cannot be a positive attribute, necessity must be negative. Unfortunately, the passage cuts off before the full argument is completed, but the initial insight is clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the fragment
Read the available Arabic and translation. Note that the proof starts by stating that necessity is predicated of non-existence.
The argument is incomplete due to a page break.
2
Understand the premise
Razi claims that when something is impossible to exist, it is necessary that it does not exist. So necessity applies to non-existent things.
3
Recognize the implication
If necessity can be predicated of non-existence, it cannot be a positive attribute (since positive attributes require existence). Thus necessity is negative.

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
Proving that Necessity is a Negative Attribute
Concludes that wujub is negative and sharing it does not cause composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessity (wujub) is considered a negative attribute in Islamic theology and why sharing it does not imply a shared essence.

Core Idea
Necessity is not a positive quality; it is the absence of possibility of non-existence.

This passage is the concluding part of a larger argument establishing that the attribute of necessity (wujub) is negative, not positive. Imam Razi emphasizes that necessity is predicated of non-existence, meaning it does not add a positive reality to the thing. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping divine simplicity and the uniqueness of God's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let the author's own words establish the conclusion before you analyze.
Notice the repeated phrase 'فثبت' (so it is established) which marks each step of the conclusion.
2
Understand 'predicated of non-existence'
Grasp what it means for an attribute to be predicated of non-existence. It means the attribute does not positively exist; it is a negation or absence.
Razi argues that a positive attribute cannot subsist in pure negation, so necessity must be negative.
3
Explore the implication for essences
If necessity is negative, then sharing it does not cause multiplicity in essences. This preserves the oneness of God and the distinctness of other necessary beings (if any).
This is a key point in defending tawḥīd against objections of composition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الثالثة محمول على لا وجود فثبت أن مفهوم الوجوب محمول على العدم، وإنما قلنا إن المحمول على العدم يمتنع أن يكون ثابتا لأنه ثبت في بدائه العقول أن قيام الصفة الموجودة بالنفي المحض محال فثبت بهذه البراهين الثلاثة أن الوجوب صفة عدمية، وثبت أن الاشتراك في الصفة العدمية لا يوجب وقوع الكثرة في الماهية، فثبت أنه لا يلزم من اشتراك الشيئين في الوجوب وقوع الاشتراك في ماهيتهما.
The third introduction: [The attribute of necessity] is predicated of non-existence, so it is established that the concept of necessity is predicated of nothingness. And we only say that what is predicated of nothingness cannot be positive, because it is established in the primary intuitions of intellects that the subsisting of a positive attribute in pure negation is impossible. So it is established by these three proofs that necessity is a negative attribute. And it is established that sharing in a negative attribute does not necessitate the occurrence of multiplicity in the essence. So it is established that from the sharing of two things in necessity, the occurrence of sharing in their essence does not follow.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is the conclusion of an argument establishing that wujub (necessity) is a negative attribute (sifa 'adamiyya). It begins by stating that the concept of necessity is predicated of non-existence, meaning it does not positively exist in the thing. The reason is that a positive attribute cannot subsist in pure negation. Therefore, necessity is not a positive attribute. Then it draws the implication: if two things share a negative attribute, that does not cause their essences to become multiple or composite. So if two beings were each necessary, their sharing in necessity does not mean they share in essence; their essences can remain distinct.

Key Terms
الوجوب
صفة عدمية
المحمول على العدم
الكثرة في الماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That necessity is a positive attribute like existence or power.
Correction: Necessity is a negative attribute; it is predicated of non-existence, meaning it does not add a positive reality to the entity.

Checkpoint
What is established by the three proofs mentioned in this passage?
A) Necessity is a positive attribute
B) Necessity is a negative attribute
C) Sharing in necessity implies sharing in essence
D) Negation cannot be predicated

Key Takeaway
Necessity is a negative attribute; sharing it does not imply a shared essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that necessity is not a positive attribute but a negation. How does this affect your understanding of God's nature? Are you willing to let go of any mental image of God having 'qualities' like created beings, and instead affirm that He is utterly simple and incomparable?
?
This passage shows that sharing a negative attribute does not imply a shared essence. If you have ever thought that God and something else could be 'necessary' in the same way, how must you correct that belief right now? What does this mean for your reliance on God alone as the only necessary being?
?
Reflect: When you say 'God is necessary,' do you feel that you are attributing something positive to Him? This lesson demands that you understand it as a negation of non-existence. Will you commit to reforming your internal speech about God, ensuring you do not unconsciously ascribe to Him the limitations of created attributes?

The Claim and First Proof: Infinite Regress
Introduction and first proof against positivity of determination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial claim that determination (ta'ayyun) is not a positive attribute and the first proof based on infinite regress.

Core Idea
Determination is not positive; otherwise, it would lead to infinite regress.

Imam Razi continues his defense of divine oneness by addressing an objection. The objector concedes that necessity is positive but denies that determination is positive. We will explore the first of four proofs showing that determination must be negative.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author first states the claim and then presents the first proof.
The passage uses logical reasoning; pay attention to the structure.
2
Identify the first proof's logic
The proof argues that if determination were positive, each determination would need another determination to distinguish it, leading to an infinite chain.
This is known as an infinite regress (tasalsul).
3
Understand why infinite regress is impossible
Infinite regress is impossible in causation because it would never terminate. The author uses this to reject the positivity of determination.

السؤال الثاني : سلمنا أن الوجوب صفة ثبوتية لكن لا نسلم أن التعين أمر ثبوتي، بل نقول : التعين ليس بأمر ثبوتي وإذا كان كذلك لا يلزم من حصول المباينة في التعين وقوع التركيب في الماهية. والذي يدل على أن التعين ليس أمرا ثبوتيًا وجوه أحدها: أن تعين كل شيء متعين غير تعين المتعين الآخر، وإلا لكان تعين كل شيء عين تعين غيره وعلى هذا التقدير يلزم أن تكون الأشياء كلها متعينة بتعين واحد، وهو محال، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : أفراد التعينات متساوية في ماهية كونها تعينا، وكل واحد من تلك الأفراد يباين الآخر بتعينه فيلزم أن يكون تعين المتعين زائدا عليه، ثم الكلام في الثاني كما في الأول فيلزم التسلسل وهو محال. وثانيها : وهو أن التعين لو كان زائدا على الذات لكان اختصاص ذلك الزائد المسمى بالتعين بهذه الذات دون تلك الذات يتوقف على امتياز هذه الذات عن تلك الذات ولكن امتياز هذه الذات عن تلك الذات يتوقف على تعين هذه الذات، وتلك الذات، فلو كان تعين هذه الذات وتعين تلك الذات معللا بذلك الزائد ووقع الدور، وإنه محال. وثالثها : لو كان التعين وصفًا زائدا على الذات لكان المتعين لم يكن في نفسه شيئًا واحداً، بل كان شيئين : أحدهما : تلك الذات والثاني : الصفة والمسماة بالتعين القائمة بالذات، وإذا كانا شيئين ولكل واحد منهما تعين فلا يكون ذلك الشيء اثنين بل أربعة، ثم لكل واحد من تلك الأربعة تعين آخر، فلا يكون ذلك أربعة بل ثمانية، وهلم جرا، فيلزم من ذلك أن الشيء الذي حكمنا عليه بأنه واحد ليس بواحد بل أعداد غير متناهية، وذلك محال؛ لأن الواحد لا يكون عدداً، وأيضًا فإن الكثرة عبارة عن مجموع الوحدات فلا بد هناك من وحدة، لكن تلك الوحدة لها تعين فلا تكون الوحدة وحدة، هذا خلف. رابعها : أن التعين عبارة عن أنه ليس هو ذلك الآخر، ومفهوم أنه ليس هو الآخر مفهوم سلبي لا ثبوتي. فثبت بهذه الدلائل : أن التعين يمتنع أن يكون أمرًا ثبوتيًا. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لمَ لا يجوز أن يقال : الشيئان اللذان يكون كل واحد منهما واجبًا لذاته أنهما يتشاركان في تمام الماهية - وهي الوجوب ـ ويتباينان بالتعين، إلا أن التعين أمر عدمي وعلى هذا التقدير لا يلزم وقوع التركيب في الماهية؟
The second question: We grant that necessity is a positive attribute, but we do not grant that determination (ta'ayyun) is a positive matter. Rather we say: determination is not a positive matter. If that is the case, then difference in determination does not entail composition in the essence. What indicates that determination is not positive are several points: First: that the determination of each determined thing is different from the determination of another determined thing, otherwise all would have one determination, impossible. Having established this, we say: the individual determinations are equal in the essence of being determination, and each individual differs from the other by its determination, so the determination of the determined would be additional, then the same for the second, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. Second: if determination were additional to the essence, the specification of that additional attribute called determination with this essence rather than that essence would depend on the distinction of this essence from that essence, but the distinction of this essence from that essence depends on the determination of this essence and that essence. So if the determination of this essence and that essence were caused by that additional attribute, circularity would occur, which is impossible. Third: if determination were an attribute additional to the essence, the determined would not be one thing in itself but two: that essence and the attribute called determination subsisting in the essence. If they are two and each has a determination, it becomes four, then each of those four has another determination, so it becomes eight, and so on. Hence the thing we judged to be one is not one but infinite numbers, impossible; because the one is not a number, and multiplicity is a collection of units, so there must be a unity, but that unity has a determination, so it is not a unity—this is a contradiction. Fourth: determination is the expression that it is not that other, and the concept that it is not the other is a negative concept, not a positive one. Thus it is established by these proofs that determination cannot be a positive matter. And if this is established, we say: why is it not permissible to say that two things, each necessary by itself, share in the complete essence (which is necessity) and differ in determination, given that determination is negative, and on this assumption composition in the essence does not occur?
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection against the argument for divine oneness. The objector concedes that necessity could be positive but argues that ta'ayyun (determination, individuation) is not a positive attribute. If determination is negative, then two necessary beings could share the positive essence of necessity while differing only in a negative attribute, and no real composition arises. Four proofs are given to show determination is negative: 1) each thing's determination is unique, otherwise all would have one determination; 2) if determination were additional, circularity would result because the distinction of the essence would depend on determination and vice versa; 3) infinite regress of determinations; 4) determination is simply the negative notion of 'not being the other'. Then the objector concludes that if determination is negative, sharing in positive essence and differing in negative attribute does not cause composition.

Key Terms
التعين
صفة ثبوتية
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Determination is a positive, real attribute of a thing.
Correction: The proof shows that if it were positive, infinite regress would result, so it must be negative.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the first proof?
A) Determination is a positive attribute.
B) Determination leads to infinite regress if positive.
C) Determination is the same for all things.
D) Determination causes composition in the essence.

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows that determination cannot be positive because it would lead to an infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument shows that your own uniqueness (determination) is not an added property but inherent to your essence. Do you often seek external labels or achievements to define who you are? How can you embrace your essence without these additions, trusting in the simple fact that you are created by God?
?
If determination were positive, it would lead to an infinite regress. In your spiritual life, do you sometimes feel that you need to 'add' more and more qualities to be acceptable to God? How does this proof free you from that endless chase and point to reliance on the Divine?

Second and Third Proofs: Circularity and Infinite Divisibility
Second and third proofs that determination is not positive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two additional proofs that determination cannot be a positive attribute: the circularity argument and the argument that it leads to infinite divisibility of the one.

Core Idea
If determination were additional, it would cause circularity or break the unity of a thing into infinite parts.

Imam Razi presents two more arguments against the positivity of determination. The first shows that if determination were additional, it would require a prior distinction leading to circularity. The second shows that it would fragment a single entity into an infinite number of parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof
Focus on the circularity: the assignment of determination depends on distinction, which depends on determination.
Circularity is impossible in logical reasoning.
2
Read the third proof
Notice how each additional determination multiplies the number of entities, leading to infinite parts.
This challenges the unity of a thing.
3
Reflect on the implications
Both proofs show that a positive determination leads to absurd consequences, reinforcing that it must be negative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثاني : سلمنا أن الوجوب صفة ثبوتية لكن لا نسلم أن التعين أمر ثبوتي، بل نقول : التعين ليس بأمر ثبوتي وإذا كان كذلك لا يلزم من حصول المباينة في التعين وقوع التركيب في الماهية. والذي يدل على أن التعين ليس أمرا ثبوتيًا وجوه أحدها: أن تعين كل شيء متعين غير تعين المتعين الآخر، وإلا لكان تعين كل شيء عين تعين غيره وعلى هذا التقدير يلزم أن تكون الأشياء كلها متعينة بتعين واحد، وهو محال، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : أفراد التعينات متساوية في ماهية كونها تعينا، وكل واحد من تلك الأفراد يباين الآخر بتعينه فيلزم أن يكون تعين المتعين زائدا عليه، ثم الكلام في الثاني كما في الأول فيلزم التسلسل وهو محال. وثانيها : وهو أن التعين لو كان زائدا على الذات لكان اختصاص ذلك الزائد المسمى بالتعين بهذه الذات دون تلك الذات يتوقف على امتياز هذه الذات عن تلك الذات ولكن امتياز هذه الذات عن تلك الذات يتوقف على تعين هذه الذات، وتلك الذات، فلو كان تعين هذه الذات وتعين تلك الذات معللا بذلك الزائد ووقع الدور، وإنه محال. وثالثها : لو كان التعين وصفًا زائدا على الذات لكان المتعين لم يكن في نفسه شيئًا واحداً، بل كان شيئين : أحدهما : تلك الذات والثاني : الصفة والمسماة بالتعين القائمة بالذات، وإذا كانا شيئين ولكل واحد منهما تعين فلا يكون ذلك الشيء اثنين بل أربعة، ثم لكل واحد من تلك الأربعة تعين آخر، فلا يكون ذلك أربعة بل ثمانية، وهلم جرا، فيلزم من ذلك أن الشيء الذي حكمنا عليه بأنه واحد ليس بواحد بل أعداد غير متناهية، وذلك محال؛ لأن الواحد لا يكون عدداً، وأيضًا فإن الكثرة عبارة عن مجموع الوحدات فلا بد هناك من وحدة، لكن تلك الوحدة لها تعين فلا تكون الوحدة وحدة، هذا خلف. رابعها : أن التعين عبارة عن أنه ليس هو ذلك الآخر، ومفهوم أنه ليس هو الآخر مفهوم سلبي لا ثبوتي. فثبت بهذه الدلائل : أن التعين يمتنع أن يكون أمرًا ثبوتيًا. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لمَ لا يجوز أن يقال : الشيئان اللذان يكون كل واحد منهما واجبًا لذاته أنهما يتشاركان في تمام الماهية - وهي الوجوب ـ ويتباينان بالتعين، إلا أن التعين أمر عدمي وعلى هذا التقدير لا يلزم وقوع التركيب في الماهية؟
The second question: We grant that necessity is a positive attribute, but we do not grant that determination (ta'ayyun) is a positive matter. Rather we say: determination is not a positive matter. If that is the case, then difference in determination does not entail composition in the essence. What indicates that determination is not positive are several points: First: that the determination of each determined thing is different from the determination of another determined thing, otherwise all would have one determination, impossible. Having established this, we say: the individual determinations are equal in the essence of being determination, and each individual differs from the other by its determination, so the determination of the determined would be additional, then the same for the second, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. Second: if determination were additional to the essence, the specification of that additional attribute called determination with this essence rather than that essence would depend on the distinction of this essence from that essence, but the distinction of this essence from that essence depends on the determination of this essence and that essence. So if the determination of this essence and that essence were caused by that additional attribute, circularity would occur, which is impossible. Third: if determination were an attribute additional to the essence, the determined would not be one thing in itself but two: that essence and the attribute called determination subsisting in the essence. If they are two and each has a determination, it becomes four, then each of those four has another determination, so it becomes eight, and so on. Hence the thing we judged to be one is not one but infinite numbers, impossible; because the one is not a number, and multiplicity is a collection of units, so there must be a unity, but that unity has a determination, so it is not a unity—this is a contradiction. Fourth: determination is the expression that it is not that other, and the concept that it is not the other is a negative concept, not a positive one. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Adding determination as a positive attribute does not affect the unity of a thing.
Correction: The third proof shows that it would break unity into infinite parts.

Checkpoint
What does the third proof say would happen if determination were additional?
A) The thing would remain one.
B) The thing would become two, then four, etc., ad infinitum.
C) The thing would become nothing.
D) The thing would become a number.

Key Takeaway
The second and third proofs show that a positive determination leads to circularity or infinite parts, so it must be negative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own identity, do you assume that your 'essence' is something fixed and that your characteristics are added onto it? This lesson argues that such additive thinking leads to logical breakdowns. Where in your life might you be adding 'determinations' to your core self that cause confusion?
?
Have you ever defended a belief using circular reasoning—where your proof assumes what you are trying to prove? This lesson shows that circularity is impossible. Will you examine your own beliefs today to root out such flawed reasoning?
?
The third proof shows that adding an attribute to a unit makes it infinitely divisible. Consider your relationship with Allah: do you ever think of His attributes as separate additions to His essence, thereby undermining His absolute unity? How can you train your mind to affirm divine simplicity without falling into this trap?

The Fourth Proof and Conclusion: Determination is Negative
Fourth proof and concluding application to the question.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof that determination is a negative concept and the conclusion that two necessary beings can share essence and differ by a negative attribute.

Core Idea
Determination is simply 'not being another', a negative concept, so it cannot cause composition.

The fourth proof approaches determination from a conceptual standpoint: to be determined is to be distinct from others, which is a negation. Imam Razi then concludes that since determination is negative, two necessary beings can share a positive essence and differ only in a negative attribute, avoiding composition.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth proof
Notice that the author defines determination as 'it is not that other' – a negative concept.
2
Read the conclusion
The author applies this to the original problem: two necessary beings share essence but differ in determination, a negative attribute, so no composition.
3
Reflect on the overall argument
All four proofs together establish that determination is negative, which defends the possibility of two necessary beings without compromising unity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The second question: We grant that necessity is a positive attribute, but we do not grant that determination (ta'ayyun) is a positive matter. Rather we say: determination is not a positive matter. If that is the case, then difference in determination does not entail composition in the essence. What indicates that determination is not positive are several points: First: that the determination of each determined thing is different from the determination of another determined thing, otherwise all would have one determination, impossible. Having established this, we say: the individual determinations are equal in the essence of being determination, and each individual differs from the other by its determination, so the determination of the determined would be additional, then the same for the second, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. So if the determination of this essence and that essence were caused by that additional attribute, circularity would occur, which is impossible. Third: if determination were an attribute additional to the essence, the determined would not be one thing in itself but two: that essence and the attribute called determination subsisting in the essence. If they are two and each has a determination, it becomes four, then each of those four has another determination, so it becomes eight, and so on. Fourth: determination is the expression that it is not that other, and the concept that it is not the other is a negative concept, not a positive one. According to the fourth proof, what is the meaning of determination?
A) A positive attribute of a thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that any difference between two things must be a positive distinction? How does this lesson's proof that determination is merely negative challenge your natural inclination to think in terms of added attributes? Will you now examine your assumptions about how things differ, especially regarding Allah's oneness?
?
If determination is just 'not being the other', what does that tell you about your own identity? In what ways do you define yourself by what you are not, rather than by what you are? How can you shift your self-understanding to focus on positive attributes of iman rather than mere negation?
?
This proof shows that two necessary beings can share essence and differ only negatively. Does your heart truly accept that Allah's essence is utterly simple, with no composition even conceptually? If there is any lingering doubt, what step of this argument do you need to internalize more deeply to remove it?
